<p><b>Choi Seung-hyun</b> (<a href="/wiki/Hangul" title="Hangul">Hangul</a>: <span lang="ko-Hang">최승현</span>; born November 4, 1987),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Russell2014_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Russell2014-2">[2]</a></sup> better known by his stage name <b>T.O.P</b>, is a South Korean rapper, singer-songwriter and actor. He is a member of the South Korean K-Pop group <a href="/wiki/Big_Bang_(South_Korean_band)" title="Big Bang (South Korean band)">Big Bang</a> and has also participated in various dramas and films, such as <i><a href="/wiki/I_Am_Sam_(TV_series)" title="I Am Sam (TV series)">I Am Sam</a></i> (2007), <i><a href="/wiki/Iris_(TV_series)" title="Iris (TV series)">Iris</a></i> (2009), <i><a href="/wiki/19-Nineteen" title="19-Nineteen">Nineteen</a></i> (2009), <i><a href="/wiki/71:_Into_the_Fire" title="71: Into the Fire">71: Into the Fire</a></i> (2010), <i><a href="/wiki/Commitment_(film)" title="Commitment (film)">Commitment</a></i> (2013), <i><a href="/wiki/Tazza:_The_Hidden_Card" title="Tazza: The Hidden Card">Tazza: The Hidden Card</a></i> (2014) and <i><a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Out_of_Control" title="Out of Control">Out of Control</a></i> (2016).</p>
<p>Jeff Benjamin of <a href="/wiki/Billboard_K-Town" title="Billboard K-Town">Billboard K-Town</a> columnist noted that T.O.P is well known for his low-bass timbre rapping.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_and_career">Life and career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=T.O.P_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Life and career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2005.E2.80.9306:_Early_life_and_debut_with_Big_Bang">2005–06: Early life and debut with Big Bang</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=T.O.P_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 2005–06: Early life and debut with Big Bang">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Big_Bang_(South_Korean_band)" title="Big Bang (South Korean band)">Big Bang (South Korean band)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Big_Bang_In_Thailand.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Big_Bang_In_Thailand.JPG/220px-Big_Bang_In_Thailand.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Big_Bang_In_Thailand.JPG/330px-Big_Bang_In_Thailand.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Big_Bang_In_Thailand.JPG/440px-Big_Bang_In_Thailand.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Big_Bang_In_Thailand.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Big_Bang_(South_Korean_band)" title="Big Bang (South Korean band)">Big Bang</a> at MTV Fast Forward, Thailand, December 2007</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Prior to his involvement with <a href="/wiki/YG_Entertainment" title="YG Entertainment">YG Entertainment</a>, Seung-hyun was an underground rapper under the name of Tempo, and a childhood friend of <a href="/wiki/G-Dragon" title="G-Dragon">G-Dragon</a>, another member and leader of Big Bang.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E6.96.B0.EC.8A.A4.ED.83.80.EA.B3.A0.EB.B0.B1_.EC.A7.80.EB.93.9C.EB.9E.98.EA.B3.A4.E2.91.A5.27.EB.B9.85.EB.B1.85.27_.EB.B3.84.EB.AA.85.EC.9D.80_.27.EC.96.B4.E3.85.89.E3.85.85.EC.BC.80.ED.95.B4.27.EC.98.80.EC.A3.A0_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-.E6.96.B0.EC.8A.A4.ED.83.80.EA.B3.A0.EB.B0.B1_.EC.A7.80.EB.93.9C.EB.9E.98.EA.B3.A4.E2.91.A5.27.EB.B9.85.EB.B1.85.27_.EB.B3.84.EB.AA.85.EC.9D.80_.27.EC.96.B4.E3.85.89.E3.85.85.EC.BC.80.ED.95.B4.27.EC.98.80.EC.A3.A0-4">[4]</a></sup> G-Dragon stated that the two were "neighborhood friend[s] from middle school" and would often dance and rap together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dance_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-dance-5">[5]</a></sup> Although G-Dragon later moved away and the two "became distant", he contacted Seung-hyun again when YG Entertainment was scouting for candidates to create a boy band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dance_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-dance-5">[5]</a></sup> The pair recorded several demos and sent them to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yang_Hyun_Suk" title="Yang Hyun Suk">Yang Hyun Suk</a>, CEO of YG Entertainment, who later asked Seung-hyun to audition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E6.96.B0.EC.8A.A4.ED.83.80.EA.B3.A0.EB.B0.B1_.EC.A7.80.EB.93.9C.EB.9E.98.EA.B3.A4.E2.91.A5.27.EB.B9.85.EB.B1.85.27_.EB.B3.84.EB.AA.85.EC.9D.80_.27.EC.96.B4.E3.85.89.E3.85.85.EC.BC.80.ED.95.B4.27.EC.98.80.EC.A3.A0_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-.E6.96.B0.EC.8A.A4.ED.83.80.EA.B3.A0.EB.B0.B1_.EC.A7.80.EB.93.9C.EB.9E.98.EA.B3.A4.E2.91.A5.27.EB.B9.85.EB.B1.85.27_.EB.B3.84.EB.AA.85.EC.9D.80_.27.EC.96.B4.E3.85.89.E3.85.85.EC.BC.80.ED.95.B4.27.EC.98.80.EC.A3.A0-4">[4]</a></sup> Seung-hyun was initially rejected by the record label, which deemed him too "chubby" to fit the "idealistic version" of an idol.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E6.96.B0.EC.8A.A4.ED.83.80.EA.B3.A0.EB.B0.B1_.EC.A7.80.EB.93.9C.EB.9E.98.EA.B3.A4.E2.91.A5.27.EB.B9.85.EB.B1.85.27_.EB.B3.84.EB.AA.85.EC.9D.80_.27.EC.96.B4.E3.85.89.E3.85.85.EC.BC.80.ED.95.B4.27.EC.98.80.EC.A3.A0_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-.E6.96.B0.EC.8A.A4.ED.83.80.EA.B3.A0.EB.B0.B1_.EC.A7.80.EB.93.9C.EB.9E.98.EA.B3.A4.E2.91.A5.27.EB.B9.85.EB.B1.85.27_.EB.B3.84.EB.AA.85.EC.9D.80_.27.EC.96.B4.E3.85.89.E3.85.85.EC.BC.80.ED.95.B4.27.EC.98.80.EC.A3.A0-4">[4]</a></sup> Seung-hyun later stated that he "went home and exercised really hard because I wanted to join YG Entertainment."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E6.96.B0.EC.8A.A4.ED.83.80.EA.B3.A0.EB.B0.B1_.EC.A7.80.EB.93.9C.EB.9E.98.EA.B3.A4.E2.91.A5.27.EB.B9.85.EB.B1.85.27_.EB.B3.84.EB.AA.85.EC.9D.80_.27.EC.96.B4.E3.85.89.E3.85.85.EC.BC.80.ED.95.B4.27.EC.98.80.EC.A3.A0_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-.E6.96.B0.EC.8A.A4.ED.83.80.EA.B3.A0.EB.B0.B1_.EC.A7.80.EB.93.9C.EB.9E.98.EA.B3.A4.E2.91.A5.27.EB.B9.85.EB.B1.85.27_.EB.B3.84.EB.AA.85.EC.9D.80_.27.EC.96.B4.E3.85.89.E3.85.85.EC.BC.80.ED.95.B4.27.EC.98.80.EC.A3.A0-4">[4]</a></sup> Six months later, he returned for another audition and was signed on. He reportedly lost 20 kg in 40 days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.E6.96.B0.EC.8A.A4.ED.83.80.EA.B3.A0.EB.B0.B1_.EC.A7.80.EB.93.9C.EB.9E.98.EA.B3.A4.E2.91.A5.27.EB.B9.85.EB.B1.85.27_.EB.B3.84.EB.AA.85.EC.9D.80_.27.EC.96.B4.E3.85.89.E3.85.85.EC.BC.80.ED.95.B4.27.EC.98.80.EC.A3.A0_4-4"><a href="#cite_note-.E6.96.B0.EC.8A.A4.ED.83.80.EA.B3.A0.EB.B0.B1_.EC.A7.80.EB.93.9C.EB.9E.98.EA.B3.A4.E2.91.A5.27.EB.B9.85.EB.B1.85.27_.EB.B3.84.EB.AA.85.EC.9D.80_.27.EC.96.B4.E3.85.89.E3.85.85.EC.BC.80.ED.95.B4.27.EC.98.80.EC.A3.A0-4">[4]</a></sup> Choi Seung-hyun was given the stage name of T.O.P. (Korean: 탑) by fellow YG artist Se7en. He became one of the two rappers in the group Big Bang, alongside G-Dragon. The two were paired with four others: <a href="/wiki/Taeyang" title="Taeyang">Taeyang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daesung" title="Daesung">Daesung</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seungri" title="Seungri">Seungri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jang_Hyun-seung" title="Jang Hyun-seung">Jang Hyun-seung</a> and a documentation of their training was aired to promote them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Big_Bang_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Big_Bang-6">[6]</a></sup> Later <a href="/wiki/Hyun-seung" title="Hyun-seung">Hyun-seung</a> was dropped by the record label, and Big Bang made its official debut with five members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.27.EC.A4.80.EB.B9.84.EB.90.9C_.EA.B7.B8.EB.A3.B9.27_.EB.B9.85.EB.B1.85.2C_.EB.8C.80.ED.8F.AD.EB.B0.9C_.EC.98.88.EA.B3.A0_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-.27.EC.A4.80.EB.B9.84.EB.90.9C_.EA.B7.B8.EB.A3.B9.27_.EB.B9.85.EB.B1.85.2C_.EB.8C.80.ED.8F.AD.EB.B0.9C_.EC.98.88.EA.B3.A0-7">[7]</a></sup> Their first album, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Since_2007" title="Since 2007">Since 2007</a>,</i> was a fair success,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Album_Sales_For_The_Month_of_February_2007_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Album_Sales_For_The_Month_of_February_2007-8">[8]</a></sup> and included T.O.P.'s first solo song "Big Boy." The group achieved mainstream success with the release of the song "Lies" (Korean: 거짓말; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revised_Romanization" title="Revised Romanization">Revised Romanization</a>: <i>Geojitmal</i>) from their 2007 mini-album <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Always_(Big_Bang_album)" title="Always (Big Bang album)">Always</a></i>, which topped several charts upon its release. The singles, "Last Farewell" (Korean: 마지막 인사; Revised Romanization: <i>Majimak Insa</i>) from the mini-album <i><a href="/wiki/Hot_Issue_(EP)" title="Hot Issue (EP)">Hot Issue</a></i> and "Day by Day" (Korean: 하루하루; Revised Romanization: <i>Haru Haru</i>) from <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stand_Up_(Big_Bang_album)" title="Stand Up (Big Bang album)">Stand Up</a></i>, became chart-toppers as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.EB.B9.85.EB.B1.85_.EC.A5.AC.ED.81.AC.EC.98.A8.EC.B0.A8.ED.8A.B8_8.EC.A3.BC_.EC.97.B0.EC.86.8D_1.EC.9C.84_.EA.B8.B0.EC.97.BC.2C_JOO.EB.8F.84_2.EC.A3.BC.EB.A7.8C.EC.97.90_7.EC.9C.84_.EC.A7.84.EC.9E.85_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-.EB.B9.85.EB.B1.85_.EC.A5.AC.ED.81.AC.EC.98.A8.EC.B0.A8.ED.8A.B8_8.EC.A3.BC_.EC.97.B0.EC.86.8D_1.EC.9C.84_.EA.B8.B0.EC.97.BC.2C_JOO.EB.8F.84_2.EC.A3.BC.EB.A7.8C.EC.97.90_7.EC.9C.84_.EC.A7.84.EC.9E.85-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Big_Bang.27s_.27Day_by_Day.27_Sweeps_J-POP_Charts_for_Four_Weeks_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Big_Bang.27s_.27Day_by_Day.27_Sweeps_J-POP_Charts_for_Four_Weeks-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2007.E2.80.9310:_Solo_career_development.2C_move_into_acting.2C_and_GD.26TOP">2007–10: Solo career development, move into acting, and <i>GD&amp;TOP</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=T.O.P_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2007–10: Solo career development, move into acting, and GD&amp;TOP">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GD%26TOP_performance_at_Big_Bang%27s_Big_Show,_2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2488" data-file-width="3740" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/GD%26TOP_performance_at_Big_Bang%27s_Big_Show%2C_2011.jpg/220px-GD%26TOP_performance_at_Big_Bang%27s_Big_Show%2C_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/GD%26TOP_performance_at_Big_Bang%27s_Big_Show%2C_2011.jpg/330px-GD%26TOP_performance_at_Big_Bang%27s_Big_Show%2C_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/GD%26TOP_performance_at_Big_Bang%27s_Big_Show%2C_2011.jpg/440px-GD%26TOP_performance_at_Big_Bang%27s_Big_Show%2C_2011.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GD%26TOP_performance_at_Big_Bang%27s_Big_Show,_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
T.O.P performing with <a href="/wiki/G-Dragon" title="G-Dragon">G-Dragon</a> in 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following the release of the band's albums and singles, T.O.P. began working on his solo career. In April 2007, he was featured with fellow Big Bang members Taeyang and G-Dragon on singer <a href="/wiki/Lexy_(singer)" title="Lexy (singer)">Lexy</a>'s single "Super Fly" for her album <i>Rush</i>. Later that summer, he appeared as an actor in Red Roc's "Hello" music video.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.EB.B9.85.EB.B1.85_8.EC.9B.94_.EC.8B.A0.EB.B3.B4_.EB.B0.9C.EB.A7.A4.2C_.ED.83.9C.EC.96.91_.EC.86.94.EB.A1.9C_.EB.8D.B0.EB.B7.94.EB.8A.94_.EB.AF.B8.EC.A0.95_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-.EB.B9.85.EB.B1.85_8.EC.9B.94_.EC.8B.A0.EB.B3.B4_.EB.B0.9C.EB.A7.A4.2C_.ED.83.9C.EC.96.91_.EC.86.94.EB.A1.9C_.EB.8D.B0.EB.B7.94.EB.8A.94_.EB.AF.B8.EC.A0.95-11">[11]</a></sup> He later became the first member of Big Bang to venture into acting, starring in the <a href="/wiki/Korean_Broadcasting_System" title="Korean Broadcasting System">KBS2</a> drama <i><a href="/wiki/I_Am_Sam_(TV_series)" title="I Am Sam (TV series)">I Am Sam</a>,</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Choi_Seung_Hyun_YG_Profile_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Choi_Seung_Hyun_YG_Profile-1">[1]</a></sup> portraying the school's top fighter, Chae Musin. He also became a host of <a href="/wiki/Munhwa_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Munhwa Broadcasting Corporation">MBC</a>'s music program <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Music_Core" title="Music Core">Music Core</a></i>.</p>
<p>In 2008, he collaborated with label-mate <a href="/wiki/Gummy_(singer)" title="Gummy (singer)">Gummy</a> on the song "I'm Sorry" for her album <i>Comfort</i>, veteran singer <a href="/wiki/Uhm_Jung-hwa" title="Uhm Jung-hwa">Uhm Jung-hwa</a> for her single "D.I.S.C.O." and ZiA for her single "I Only See You". That same year, he was also admitted to <a href="/wiki/Dankook_University" title="Dankook University">Dankook University</a>, to the theatre department.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2009, T.O.P. returned to acting, playing the assassin Vick in the critically acclaimed<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRISpopular_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-IRISpopular-13">[13]</a></sup> Korean television drama <i><a href="/wiki/Iris_(TV_series)" title="Iris (TV series)">Iris</a>.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IRISannounce_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-IRISannounce-14">[14]</a></sup> He also recorded the song "Hallelujah" for the drama's soundtrack with Taeyang and G-Dragon. Following <i>Iris</i>, T.O.P. starred in the suspense film <i><a href="/wiki/19-Nineteen" title="19-Nineteen">19-Nineteen</a></i> along with fellow member <a href="/wiki/Seungri" title="Seungri">Seungri</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-My19_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-My19-15">[15]</a></sup> The duo released the single "Because" for the movie's soundtrack.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GD_%26_T.O.P_2010.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3509" data-file-width="5071" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/GD_%26_T.O.P_2010.jpg/220px-GD_%26_T.O.P_2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/GD_%26_T.O.P_2010.jpg/330px-GD_%26_T.O.P_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/GD_%26_T.O.P_2010.jpg/440px-GD_%26_T.O.P_2010.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GD_%26_T.O.P_2010.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
GD &amp; TOP promotional photo shoot</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2010, T.O.P starred in the war drama film <i><a href="/wiki/71:_Into_the_Fire" title="71: Into the Fire">71: Into the Fire</a></i>. His performance was well-received, earning him several Best New Actor awards at local award giving bodies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2010_Grand_Bell_win_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-2010_Grand_Bell_win-16">[16]</a></sup> The movie also gained 1 million views in a week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Actor_Kwon_Sang-woo_injured_while_filming_fight_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Actor_Kwon_Sang-woo_injured_while_filming_fight-17">[17]</a></sup> Simultaneously, T.O.P began to prepare for his solo musical debut.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.ED.83.91-.EB.8C.80.EC.84.B1.2C_.EB.B9.85.EB.B1.85_.EC.BD.98.EC.84.9C.ED.8A.B8.EC.84.9C_.EC.86.94.EB.A1.9C.EA.B3.A1_.EC.B2.AB_.EA.B3.B5.EA.B0.9C_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-.ED.83.91-.EB.8C.80.EC.84.B1.2C_.EB.B9.85.EB.B1.85_.EC.BD.98.EC.84.9C.ED.8A.B8.EC.84.9C_.EC.86.94.EB.A1.9C.EA.B3.A1_.EC.B2.AB_.EA.B3.B5.EA.B0.9C-18">[18]</a></sup> During Big Bang's Big Show concert in January 2010, T.O.P. performed his new single "Turn It Up".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.EB.B9.85.EB.B1.85_.ED.83.91_.EC.BD.98.EC.84.9C.ED.8A.B8.EC.84.9C_.EC.B2.AB_.EC.86.94.EB.A1.9C.EA.B3.A1_.EB.AE.A4.EB.B9.84_.EA.B9.9C.EC.A7.9D_.EA.B3.B5.EA.B0.9C_.E2.80.98.EC.98.AC_.EC.83.81.EB.B0.98.EA.B8.B0_.ED.99.9C.EB.8F.99.E2.80.99_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-.EB.B9.85.EB.B1.85_.ED.83.91_.EC.BD.98.EC.84.9C.ED.8A.B8.EC.84.9C_.EC.B2.AB_.EC.86.94.EB.A1.9C.EA.B3.A1_.EB.AE.A4.EB.B9.84_.EA.B9.9C.EC.A7.9D_.EA.B3.B5.EA.B0.9C_.E2.80.98.EC.98.AC_.EC.83.81.EB.B0.98.EA.B8.B0_.ED.99.9C.EB.8F.99.E2.80.99-19">[19]</a></sup> He became the first Korean artist to have his song released worldwide on <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a>.</p>
<p>In November 2010, YG Entertainment announced T.O.P and bandmate <a href="/wiki/G-Dragon" title="G-Dragon">G-Dragon</a> would release a collaboration album under the name <a href="/wiki/GD_%26_TOP" title="GD &amp; TOP">GD &amp; TOP</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-English_KBS_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-English_KBS-20">[20]</a></sup> Preceding the release of the album, the duo held a worldwide premiere showcase for their album at Times Square in Yeongdeungpo of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seoul,_South_Korea" title="Seoul, South Korea">Seoul, South Korea</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Showcase1_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Showcase1-21">[21]</a></sup> which was also broadcast live on YouTube.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Showcase2_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Showcase2-22">[22]</a></sup> To promote their album, the duo released three singles: "High High," "Oh Yeah," and "Knock out."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-singles_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-singles-23">[23]</a></sup> All three singles preceded the release of the album. The singles attained commercial successes: "Knock Out" was a chart topper<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JoongAng_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-JoongAng-24">[24]</a></sup> while "Oh Yeah" and "High High" both peaked at No. 2 and No. 3 respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10asia_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-10asia-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10asia2_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-10asia2-26">[26]</a></sup> The album was released on Christmas Eve, and debuted at number one<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gaon_gd.26top_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gaon_gd.26top-27">[27]</a></sup> with pre-orders of 200,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sales_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sales-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011.E2.80.93present:_Continued_acting_and_military_service">2011–present: Continued acting and military service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=T.O.P_(rapper)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2011–present: Continued acting and military service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:T.O.P_2012_3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1715" data-file-width="1209" height="312" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/T.O.P_2012_3.jpg/220px-T.O.P_2012_3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/T.O.P_2012_3.jpg/330px-T.O.P_2012_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/T.O.P_2012_3.jpg/440px-T.O.P_2012_3.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:T.O.P_2012_3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
T.O.P in 2012</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2012, T.O.P starred in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Commitment_(film)" title="Commitment (film)">Commitment</a></i> (also known as <i>Alumni</i>), playing the son of a North Korean spy who is falsely accused.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> While filming a combat scene for the movie, he injured the back of his hand on a glass fragment and was later admitted to the hospital for surgery. For his role, he won the Rookie Award at the Asia Star Awards, held during the <a href="/wiki/Busan_International_Film_Festival" title="Busan International Film Festival">Busan International Film Festival</a>.</p>
<p>T.O.P was named one of the hottest sex symbols in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> In November, he released a digital single, "Doom Dada"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> The song was performed for the first time at the Mnet Asian Music Awards 2013 in Hong Kong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> "Doom Dada" earned the #1 position on <a href="/wiki/Dazed" title="Dazed">Dazed</a> magazine's Top 10 K-Pop tracks of 2013, where it was called "inviting and alienating... it's K-Pop but sly, frenetic and slippery."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> He later featured on English artist <a href="/wiki/Pixie_Lott" title="Pixie Lott">Pixie Lott</a>'s Japanese album alongside G-Dragon for the song "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dancing_on_My_Own_(Pixie_Lott_song)" title="Dancing on My Own (Pixie Lott song)">Dancing on My Own</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, T.O.P starred in the gambling film <i><a href="/wiki/Tazza:_The_Hidden_Card" title="Tazza: The Hidden Card">Tazza: The Hidden Card</a></i>, based on the <a href="/wiki/Tajja" title="Tajja">manhwa of the same name</a>.</p>
<p>After debuting as a furniture designer in 2015 in collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Vitra_(furniture)" title="Vitra (furniture)">Vitra</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> he was awarded the Visual Culture Award at the Prudential Eye Awards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>Also in 2015, he starred in CJ E&amp;M's web drama <i>The Secret Message</i> alongside Japanese actress <a href="/wiki/Juri_Ueno" title="Juri Ueno">Juri Ueno</a>. He released the single "Hi Haruka" as part of the drama's soundtrack.</p>
<p>In 2016, T.O.P was cast in the German-Chinese film <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Out_of_Control_(upcoming_film)" title="Out of Control (upcoming film)">Out of Control</a></i> alongside Hong Kong actress <a href="/wiki/Cecilia_Cheung" title="Cecilia Cheung">Cecilia Cheung</a>. The movie is scheduled for release in China in December 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frater_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Frater-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>T.O.P will begin his two-year <a href="/wiki/Conscription_in_South_Korea" title="Conscription in South Korea">mandatory military service</a> on February 9, 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
